co-operate secretly: to have a secret understanding." He also included definitions of connive, a synonym of the verb collude, such as "to deliberately ignore; to overlook; to disregard; to pass over; to take no notice of; to turn a blind eye; to wink; to excuse; to condone; to look the other way; to let something ride." Nuala (now Baroness) O'Loan, the first police ombudsman for Northern Ireland, adopted the definitions of Lord Stevens and Peter Cory to examine whether there had been collusion in the murder of Raymond McCord jnr, concluding that there had been collusion. Al Hutchinson, her successor as police ombudsman, applied a less broad definition in his report on the attack on McGurk's Bar, stating that the essence of collusion requires an agreement or arrangement between individuals or organizations to achieve an unlawful or improper purpose. Sir Christopher de Silva also provided a working definition of collusion, considering it to involve agreements, arrangements, or actions intended to achieve unlawful, improper, fraudulent, or underhand objectives, and deliberately turning a blind eye or ignoring improper or unlawful activity. Finally, Irish judge Peter Smithwick provided a similar definition of collusion, considering it to involve both the commission of an act and an omission or failure to act.  # Output (a): The article discusses the varying definitions of collusion provided by different individuals during the conflict in Northern Ireland. Key figures such as Sir John Stevens, Lord Stevens, Peter Cory, Nuala O'Loan, Al Hutchinson, Sir Christopher de Silva, and Peter Smithwick offer distinct perspectives on the term. Stevens' definition encompasses a range of actions, from neglect to direct involvement by agents. Cory expands on the definitions of connive, which includes terms like "to deliberately ignore" or "to turn a blind eye." O'Loan and de Silva both adopt Stevens and Cory's definitions to assess instances of collusion, while Hutchinson opts for a narrower definition that requires an agreement or arrangement to achieve an unlawful or improper purpose. Smithwick's definition includes both the commission of an act and an omission or failure to act, emphasizing the importance of deliberate actions or inactions.  Differences Identification: 1. Today, MercadoLibre is a household name across Latin America, operating in 12 countries and being the most visited ecommerce website in the region. It has 109.6 million registered users and generated $473m in annual revenues last year. In 2001, eBay bought a 19.5% stake in MercadoLibre, pledging not to enter Latin America for at least five years, allowing MercadoLibre to dominate the region. Galperin initially intended to become a professional rugby player but instead studied finance and worked for YPF before founding MercadoLibre. The company's growth has been robust despite tough economic conditions, including the bursting of the dot.com bubble and Argentina's default on its international debt. MercadoLibre's success can be attributed to its reliance on the growth of broadband and mobile phones, which have seen fast internet adoption in every country in Latin America. These reforms include the creation of a new political party, the Prosperity Party, and the removal of key Tigrayan government leaders accused of corruption and repression. The move has been seen as an attempt to dismantle Ethiopia's federal system, which has been in place since 1994 and gives different ethnic groups control over the affairs of 10 regions. The Tigray People's Liberation Front (TPLF), which was influential in setting up the federal system and led the coalition government for 27 years, has been particularly opposed to these reforms, viewing them as an attempt to undermine the federal system and centralize power. The conflict between the central government and Tigray escalated in September when Tigray held its own regional election, defying the central government's decision to postpone national elections due to the coronavirus pandemic. The central government has since suspended funding for Tigray and cut ties with its administration, which has declared a "declaration of war". The political reforms have thus far had a significant impact on the Tigray region, leading to a deepening rift between the central government and Tigray and potentially exacerbating ethnic tensions in the country.  # Output (a): Ethiopian Prime Minister Abiy Ahmed has pursued a series of political reforms since taking office in 2018, which have had a significant impact on the Tigray region. Output (a) uses "The quality of the items has surprised researchers, as they were most likely made for kings and their elite warriors," while Output (b) uses "The quality of items has also surprised researchers, as they were most likely made for kings and their elite warriors." 4. Output (a) uses "providing archaeological proof of the elite warriors mentioned in poems such as Beowulf," while Output (b) uses "This has provided archaeological proof of the elite warriors mentioned in poems such as Beowulf."  Explanation and Rationale: In this case, both Output (a) and Output (b) provide a summary of the key findings from the Staffordshire Hoard that have taught us about the Anglo-Saxons. However, Output (a) provides a more detailed and comprehensive summary, including the discovery timeline, the number of items found, and the specific techniques used by the Anglo-Saxons. Output (b), while also providing relevant information, lacks the detail and specificity of Output (a). Additionally, Output (a) provides a clearer connection between the quality of the items and the archaeological proof of the elite warriors mentioned in Beowulf.  Final Decision: Therefore, Output (a) is better.
January. VAT is now being collected at the point of sale rather than at the point of importation. This essentially means that overseas retailers sending goods to the UK are expected to register for UK VAT and account for it to HMRC if the sale value is less than €150 (£135).  A government spokesperson said the new VAT model ensures goods from EU and non-EU countries are treated in the same way and that UK businesses are not disadvantaged by competition from VAT-free imports. The new system also addresses the problem of overseas sellers failing to pay the right amount of VAT on sales of goods already in the UK at the point of sale, raising an anticipated £300m every year.  # Differences Identification: 1. Output (a) provides a brief overview of the issue, while Output (b) provides a more detailed summary of the measures taken by retailer companies. 2. Output (a) does not mention the additional charges imposed by international shipping companies, while Output (b) explicitly states this information. 3. Output (a) does not mention the anticipated £300m raised by the new VAT system every year, while Output (b) includes this detail.  # Explanation and Rationale: In terms of executing the instruction, both outputs provide information about the measures taken by retailer companies to cope with Brexit. However, Output (b) provides a more detailed summary of these measures, including the additional charges imposed by international shipping companies and the anticipated £300m raised by the new VAT system every year. This makes Output (b) a better response to the given instruction as it provides a more comprehensive overview of the issue.  # Final Decision: Therefore, Output (b) is better.
on sales of goods already in the UK at the point of sale, raising an anticipated £300m every year. "Many EU businesses which currently sell goods to UK customers will have already registered for UK VAT under existing rules and HMRC is working very closely with those who haven't to ensure they can comply with the changes."  Tackling evasion Adam French, Which? consumer rights expert, said consumers would be "frustrated" if the new VAT rules were applied in a way that causes significant inconvenience. "It's vital the government makes it clear to consumers as well as traders what the changes as a result of Brexit means for them and how they shop. It should also work to ensure UK consumers can retain access to a wide range of competitively priced and quality goods."  Output (a): Some EU specialist online retailers have said they will no longer deliver to the UK because of tax changes which came into force on 1 January. Bicycle part firm Dutch Bike Bits said from now on, it would ship to every country in the world except the UK. Another firm, Belgium-based Beer On Web, said it was now shunning the UK "due to the new Brexit measures". The companies are angry because they now face higher costs and increased bureaucracy in order to comply with UK tax authorities. However, it is unclear how many have taken the drastic step of refusing all UK orders.  At the same time, international shipping companies including Federal Express and TNT have said they are levying additional charges on shipments between the UK and the EU. They said this reflected the increased investment they had had to make in adjusting their systems to cope with Brexit.  The moves follow changes in VAT rules brought in by HM Revenue and Customs on 1 January. VAT is now being collected at the point of sale rather than at the point of importation. This essentially means that overseas retailers sending goods to the UK are expected to register for UK VAT and account for it to HMRC if the sale value is less than €150 (£135).  A government spokesperson said: "The new VAT model ensures goods from EU and non-EU countries are treated in the same way and that UK businesses are not disadvantaged by competition from VAT-free imports. "The new system also addresses the problem of overseas sellers failing to pay the right amount of VAT on sales of goods already in the UK at the point of sale, raising an anticipated £300m every year. "Many EU businesses which currently sell goods to UK customers will have already registered for UKVAT under existing rules and HMRC is working very closely with those who haven't to ensure they can comply with the changes."  Tackling evasion Adam French, Which? consumer rights expert, said consumers would be "frustrated" if the new VAT rules were applied in a way that causes significant inconvenience. "It's vital the government makes it clear to consumers as well as traders what the changes as a result of Brexit means for them and how they shop. It should also work to ensure UK consumers can retain access to a wide range of competitively priced and quality goods."Differences Identification: 1. Output (a) includes additional information about Dutch Bike Bits and Scandinavian Outdoor, which are not present in Output (b). 2. Output (b) includes a quote from a government spokesperson and a quote from Adam French, Which? consumer rights expert, which are not present in Output (a).  Explanation and Rationale: Both outputs provide a summary of the measures retailer companies have taken to cope with Brexit, but Output (b) includes additional quotes from a government spokesperson and a consumer rights expert, which provide more context and insight into the situation. While Output (a) includes more specific examples of individual companies that have stopped delivering to the UK, these examples are not necessarily representative of all EU specialist online retailers. Output (b) provides a more balanced view of the situation by including quotes from both a government spokesperson and a consumer rights expert. Therefore, Output (b) is better.  Final Decision: Therefore, Output (b) is better.

Canadian judge Peter Cory defined collusion as having a secret understanding, deliberately ignoring, overlooking, disregarding, passing over, taking no notice of, turning a blind eye, winking, excusing, condoning, looking the other way, or letting something ride. Al Hutchinson, the successor as police ombudsman, applied a less broad definition in his report on the attack on McGurk's Bar.
